enum EffectTypeEnum {
    POISON,           # Harmful to body or system
    MEDICINAL,        # Restores hp, cures effects
    PSYCHOACTIVE,     # Alters perception/thought/mood
    NUTRITIONAL,      # Provides food value/healing via nutrition
    BUFF,             # Improves stat, e.g. strength, speed
    DEBUFF,           # Temporarily decreases stat
    HEALING,          # Repairs wounds, restores health
    REVITALIZING,     # Removes fatigue or boosts stamina
    CURATIVE,         # Removes debuff or status effect
    INTOXICATING,     # Alcoholic/drunken effect
    NEUTRAL,          # No mechanical effect
    SPECIAL,          # Unique or magical effect only for rare alchemy



enum PoisonSubtypeEnum {
    CORROSIVE,       # Damages organs on contact (acid burns, necrosis)
    IRRITANT,        # Causes itchiness, swelling, general discomfort
    SYSTEMIC,        # Enters bloodstream, affects multiple organs
    NEUROTOXIC,      # Targets nervous system, paralysis, spasms
    CYANOGENIC,      # Produces cyanide; blocks oxygen, rapid suffocation
    CARDIOTOXIC,     # Affects heart and blood pressure
    HEPATOTOXIC,     # Affects liver/related metabolism
    NEPHROTOXIC,     # Affects kidneys/filtration
    GI_TRACT,        # Targets stomach/intestines, vomiting/diarrhea
    HEMOTOXIC,       # Damages blood, causes hemorrhage
    ENZYME_INHIBITOR,# Inhibits key enzymes, may block digestion/nerves
    HALLUCINOGENIC,  # Induces hallucinations, confusion
    DERMATOLOGIC,    # Skin-specific reactions (burns, blisters, rash)
    RESPIRATORY,     # Targets lungs or airway
    COAGULANT,       # Thickens blood (decreases flow)
    ANTICOAGULANT,   # Prevents blood clotting (increases bleeding)
    IMMUNOTOXIC,     # Weakens immune response
    ALLERGEN,        # Triggers allergic reaction
    METABOLIC,       # Disturbs core metabolism (hypoglycemia/hyperglycemia/shock)
    PSYCHOACTIVE,    # Alters mood/thoughts; similar to "Hallucinogenic" but less severe
    CHOLINERGIC,     # Nervous system overload (sweating, salivation, seizures)
    VASODILATOR,     # Opens blood vessels, causes blood pressure drop
    MUCOSAL,         # Damages mucous membranes (mouth, throat, gut)
    CYTOTOXIC,       # Damages cells directly, causes cell death
    RADIOTOXIC,      # Causes radiation-related harm (for monsters/magical ecology)
    SLOW_ACTING,     # Delayed onset poison
    ACUTE,           # Immediate rapid poisoning
    CUMULATIVE,      # Builds up with repeated exposure, long-term effect
}

| Action      | Typical Final Size      | Surface Area Change        | Notes / Examples                 |
|-------------|------------------------|----------------------------|----------------------------------|
| GRINDING    | 0.5–2mm fragments      | ↑↑↑ (very high)            | ground flour, spices, grain      |
| CUTTING     | 1–50mm slices/chunks   | ↑ (low–mod)                | general/mechanical cuts          |
| KNAPPING    | 10–50mm shards         | ↑ (low)                    | stone, flint toolmaking          |
| CRUSHING    | 2–10mm irregular       | ↑↑ (moderate)              | hand-broken, bruised, garlic     |
| PULVERIZING | <0.5mm powder          | ↑↑↑↑ (extremely high)      | flour, fine powders              |
| SPLITTING   | 10–100mm pieces        | ↑ (low)                    | wood/log splitting, rough break  |
| SAWING      | mm–cm thick pieces     | ↑ (low–moderate)           | sawed planks, bones              |
| SLICING     | flat (2–10mm thick)    | ↑ (minor)                  | carrot/fruit discs, bacon        |
| JULIENNING  | 1–3mm × 30–70mm rods   | ↑↑ (moderate)              | matchstick veg                   |
| CHOPPING    | 5–15mm cubes/chunks    | ↑↑ (moderate)              | rough veg, stew                  |
| DICING      | 3–8mm cubes            | ↑↑ (mod-high)              | finer than chopped               |
| MINCING     | 1–3mm bits             | ↑↑↑ (high)                 | garlic, onion, meat              |
| SHREDDING   | 2–5mm × 1–2mm strips   | ↑↑↑ (high)                 | cheese, carrots                  |
| GRATING     | 1–2mm × 2–5mm bits     | ↑↑↑ (very high)            | cheese, zest                     |
| PUREEING    | paste/liquid           | ↑↑↑↑ (extreme)             | tomato sauce, baby food          |
| MASHING     | 2–5mm soft mass        | ↑↑ (mod-high)              | potatoes, avocado                |

CLEANING (The Physical Build)
This type covers the mechanical removal of surface layers.
The Bristle Bundle:
Parts: Filaments (Wire/Fiber), Ferrule (The ring that holds them), Handle.
Logic: A multi-point contact tool for irregular surfaces.
The Flat Scraper:
Parts: Hardened Bevel (The edge), Shank, Grip.
Logic: A single-point contact tool for shearing off surface buildup.
GRIPPING (Force Multipliers)
Tools that use mechanical advantage to hold or twist.
The Pivot Assembly (Pliers/Tongs/Shears)
Parts: Fulcrum Bolt, Offset Handle, Work-Head (Jaws/Blades).
Logic: The "Grip" is just a lever-ratio calculation between the handle length and the head length.
The Screw-Clamp (Vise/C-Clamp)
Parts: Threaded Spindle, Traveling Block (The jaw that moves), Guide Rail (Prevents rotation), Fixed Stop.
Logic: Uses a Leadscrew to translate rotation into high-pressure linear clamping.
SHAPING (Abrasive/Refining)
Components that remove material or enforce geometry.
The Rotary Mandrel (Lathe/Drill)
Parts: Spindle, Drive Pulley/Crank, Chuck/Collet (The part that grips the workpiece or bit), Bearing Housing.
Logic: A high-speed rotating shaft that allows a Shaping bit to hit a workpiece evenly.
The Abrasive Surface (Files/Hones)
Parts: Hardened Face, Toothed Profile, Tang.
Logic: A surface with a higher Hardness value than the workpiece, used to "scrape" away material at a sub-millimeter level.
The Punch & Matrix (For Valves/Connectors):
Parts: Male Punch, Female Die-Plate, Guide Pins (for alignment).
Logic: These are the "Standardizers." They ensure every screw or valve-flap you make is a 1:1 physical match.
The Tap (For Internal Threads):
Parts: Threaded Flutes (The cutting teeth), Square Drive (The top for a wrench), Tapered Tip.
The Die (For External Threads/Screws):
Parts: Threaded Core, Adjustment Screw (to set depth), Die Stock (The handle frame).
PERFORATTING; The Tool: Punch & Drift or Aul.
The Parts: Hardened Point/Tip, Striking Face (the top), Tapered Body.
The Function: This is how you create the starter holes for your Rivets or the slots for Standardized Connectors in sheet metal.
SMELTING (Thermal & Material State)
Parts for containing or directing high-energy states.
The Air Displacement Unit (Bellows)
Parts: Compression Chamber (Expanding/collapsing volume), One-way Reed Valve (The flap), Directional Nozzle.
Logic: A mechanical pump used to force air (oxygen) into the Furnace to raise temperatures beyond a standard fire's limit.
The Casting Vessel (Crucible/Ladle)
Parts: Refractory Liner (Thermal resistance), Structural Shell (The frame that holds the liner), Shank (Long handle for distance from heat).
Logic: A container specifically rated to stay solid while its contents are liquid.
The Die/Matrix (Molds)
Parts: Cavity (The negative space), Alignment Pins (To ensure the two halves match), Pouring Basin.
Logic: A standardized "Negative" of a part used to replicate geometry exactly.


Fastener Shear & Stability (L/W/H Logic)
The stability of a Composite is determined by the Fastener Grade relative to the Part Dimensions.
Fastener	Physics Role	Strength Formula (Sim Logic)
Rivet	Shear Specialist	Strength = (Material_Hardness * Rivet_Area) * Vibration_Modifier(1.0)
Screw	Tension/Torque	Strength = (Thread_Depth * Clamp_Force) * Vibration_Modifier(0.8)
Stability Logic: Joint_Stability = (Sum_Fastener_Strength) / (Part_Mass * Distance_from_Center).

CRAFT-LOGIC-> SET LENTGH,WIDTH, HEIGHT

Typical Fiber/Yarn Thickness:
Sewing: Fine thread, <0.5mm (often as fine as 0.1–0.3mm)
Stitching: Slightly thicker, but still fine, 0.5mm to 1mm
Braiding: 1mm+ (cords/ropes commonly 2–8mm)
Knitting: 1.5mm (fine)–5mm (bulky); most usage 2–4mm


Formulas- 
*[note-to-self][Formulas 1. need to be organized, 2. need to be paired with heat-transfer formula, and all should be coded into a state machine.(instead of running for minor changes, its main use will be for fire and magic simulation so only intentional state changes are calculated, -ps- Consider adding a buffer script for weather-mechanic (other optionis static range rolls based on season, but math is done for simulation below. Memory constraints most likely will be the main determiner.)]

1*[Pauling Electronegativity Formula
						χA - χB = 0.102 × √Δ

							where Δ = EA-B - √(EA-A × EB-B)

						Eᴀ-ʙ: Measured bond dissociation energy of the compound AB.
						Eᴀ-ᴀ, Eʙ-ʙ: Bond dissociation energies of the homonuclear diatomic molecules A₂ and B₂.
						0.102: A conversion factor used when bond energies are expressed in kJ/mol. 
       							If energies are in kcal/mol, the factor is approximately 0.208.]

[Percent Ionic Character Formula- formula to estimate the percent ionic character of a bond based on the electronegativity difference:
					% Ionic Character = (1 - e^-0.25(χA - χB)²) × 100]


2*[Reynolds Number (\(Re\)) Used to determine *Flow-Regime*. Transition to Turbulent (chaotic/AoE) occurs when \(Re>4000\). The Formula: (Flow Type) Re = (ρ * v * L) / μ
 					ρ = (Rho): Density of the fluid (kg/m³). 
 						v = Flow velocity (m/s)[meter per sec].
 						L = Characteristic linear dimension (e.g., diameter of a pipe or length of an object) (m).
						 μ = (Mu): Dynamic viscosity of the fluid (Pa.s).]
						[Threshold: Re > 4000 = Turbulent (AoE)]


3-*[Young’s Modulus (E) - Used for Space-Anchoring and Metal Rigidity to define the limit between elastic deformation and structural failure. The Formula:  E = (F / A) / (ΔL / L) or [sigma]/[epsilon]
   [Determines: Elastic limit vs. Structural failure]
 					(F/A)[sigma] = (Stress): Force applied/ τ (tau) = Force (F) divided by the Cross-sectional Area/Contact-Area (A). The standard SI unit is the Pascal (Pa), where 1 Pa = 1 N/m²
					  	For Fluids/Gases (F) is replaced by the Hydrostatic Pressure Formula: Pressure (P) = (p)x(G)x(h)
						 ρ  (Rho): Density (kg/m³), G: Gravity, h: Depth
 						(ΔL/L)v = (Strain): Deformation ratio (change in length (ΔL) over original length (L).
 						Failure Threshold: If applied stress (sigma) exceeds the material's Yield Strength, the anchor or structure undergoes permanent failure.]
 		*[Note- Nested Formula- The change in length is calculated as: ΔL = (Force * original_length)/(Area)]

							Plastic Strain Rate (\(\.{\varepsilon }_{p}\)): used to determine how a material (like metal or dry wood) permanently deforms or "flows" when the stress exceeds the yield point. Differentiates a "dent" from a "bounce."
							ε̇ₚ = (dε / dt) - ( (1 / E) · (dσ / dt) )
							ε̇ₚ = Plastic strain rate (s⁻¹)
							dε/dt = Total strain rate (the speed of impact/compression)
							E  = Young's Modulus (Material stiffness)
							dσ/dt = Rate of change of stress (Pa/s)

							Alternative (Power Law for Metal):
							ε̇ₚ = A · σⁿ
							A = Material constant
							σ = Applied stress
							n = Stress-rate sensitivity exponent

							Tensile Energy Density (\(U\)): Used to calculate how much "Magic" or "Kinetic" energy is stored in a stretched material (like a bowstring or a grappling hook).(UNSURE IF NEEDED)
										U = 0.5 · σ · ε
										U = Energy density (J/m³)

							*Need values for each element/can add to  periodic dictionary* Ultimate Tensile Strength (\(UTS\)): The maximum stress a material can withstand before failing (snapping or breaking).
										UTS = F_max / A₀
										UTS   = Ultimate Tensile Strength (Pa)
										F_max = Maximum force recorded before fracture
										A₀ = Original cross-sectional area 

4*[Bulk Modulus (K) or (B)) Essential for Water/Space-Volume compression to calculate "Crush" damage thresholds under pressure. The Formula:  K = -V * (ΔP / ΔV)
   [Determines: Resistance to volumetric pressure]
 (V): Original volume of the space or liquid.
 (ΔP): Change in pressure (volumetric stress).[Force applied]
 (ΔV): Change in volume.Application: 
 A higher (K) means the medium is harder to "Crush." For space-volume, this determines the energy required to compress a specific area.]

5*[Wave Speed (v) Mandatory for calculating travel time and penetration for hydraulic or sonic effects The Formulas: [Frequency-Wavelength Relation - v = f * λ] [Medium-Consistency Relation/Medium-Specific Speed: (Physical Velocity) - v = squrt(√)(K/ρ) [or Fluids, Space, and Solid Aether beams]]
	Medium-Specific Speed
							v (Velocity): The speed of  travel
							f (Frequency): Pulse Oscillation Rate. Higher frequency increases penetrative power/damage.
        						(λ)(lambda)[Wavelength]: Determines the "size" or Area of the wave.
							K ([In Fluids (Air/Water): (K) is the bulk modulus/compressibility)][In Solids (Earth/Metal): (K) is (Y) - the Young’s Modulus/stiffness])	
        						ρ  (Rho): Density of the fluid (kg/m³)]

6-8*[the Dielectric Constant also known as Relative Permittivity, or κ (kappa) is a fundamental dimensionless quantity that describes how a material reacts to an electric field compared to a vacuum. [Broken into 3 Formulas]
	6- [Fundamental Permittivity Formula - (Permittivity): κ = (ε)/(ε₀)  	How the material exists in nature
		κ (Kappa): Dielectric Constant (dimensionless). 
		ε (epsilon): Absolute permittivity of the material (measured in F/m).
		ε₀ (epsilon{0}): Permittivity of free space ((approx 8.854 x 10^{-12}(F/m))). 
			 "f/m" (Farads per meter, F/m)  
		[Note for me - The primary definition of the dielectric constant is the ratio of the material's absolute permittivity to the permittivity of a vacuum.] 

	7- [Capacitance-Based Formula the dielectric constant calculated by measuring the increase in a capacitor's ability to store charge. (Capacitance): κ = C_material / C_vacuum    How much energy it stores in a device.
		C_material: Capacitance with the dielectric material between the plates.
		C_vacuum: Capacitance of the same plates with a vacuum (or air) in between
	
	8-[Electric-Field-Reduction-Formula - A dielectric material reduces the effective electric field strength inside a capacitor by a factor of κ. (Field): E_inside = E_vacuum / κ    How much electric stress it can neutralize.
		E_vacuum: Original electric field without the material.
		E_inside: Resulting field after polarization of the dielectric]

9-11*[Schwarzschild Metric (The Geometry of Gravity) - The Schwarzschild metric is the primary formula used to describe the curvature of spacetime outside a non-rotating, spherically symmetric mass. 
						It serves as the "Gravity Threshold" because it defines the Schwarzschild Radius (rs), the distance from a center of mass where the escape velocity exactly equals the speed of light
						The Threshold Calculation (rs): rs = 2GM / c²
							G = gravitational constant = 6.6743e^{-11}
							M = Total Mass of Object

						9 - The Metric Formula: SCHWARZSCHILD METRIC (Spacetime Geometry) ds² = -(1 - rs/r)c²dt² + (1 - rs/r)⁻¹dr² + r²dΩ²
   									Effect: Defines time dilation and space curvature near a mass.
								rs (Schwarzschild Radius): The critical boundary (Event Horizon)
								r: The radial distance from the center of the mass.
								c: The speed of light.
								ds² :The spacetime interval (measures the "distance" between events in 4D space).
								dt: Time interval (Time Dilation term)
								dr: Radial interval (Space Curvature term)
								dθ, dϕ: Angular coordinates (Spherical Surface terms)]

						10 - [Lorentz Factor -  Mathematical Logic: Relativistic Dilation The core calculation for temporal shift utilizes the  physics-based logic: 
								Time Dilation Formula: dt² = [Δt= [Δt₀]/[sqrt[1-(Target-Velocity(V)²/Speed of Light(C)²]], 
								where Δt₀ is the proper time of the subject and (V) is the relative velocity.
								Causality Threshold (Order): In this system, the "Order" of events is maintained by the Light Cone principle. 			
								No "Action" can precede its "Cause" unless the Velocity-Resistance (Inertia) is lowered beyond the photonic constant.
								[*Note - Δt (Delta t): The time interval measured by an observer in a different, moving reference frame (the "dilated time").
								Δt₀ (Delta t-nought): The "proper time," or the time interval measured by an observer in the same frame as the events]]

   						11 - RADIAL SPACE STRETCHING (Proper Length): dr² = [Lₚᵣₒₚₑᵣ = ∫[1/sqrt(1 - 2GM/c²r)] dr]
  								Lₚᵣₒₚₑᵣ: The actual physical distance between two points in curved space.
   								2GM/c²: This is the Schwarzschild Radius (rₛ).
   								The integral accounts for the fact that space "stretches" more intensely as you approach the gravity threshold.

12*[Gravitational Collapse Threshold (Stability Limit) - the Tolman-Oppenheimer-Volkoff (TOV) Limit defines the mass threshold at which a cold, dense object (like a neutron star) must inevitably collapse. 
							COLLAPSE THRESHOLD (Mass Limits) THE TOLMAN-OPPENHEIMER-VOLKOFF (TOV) EQUATION dP/dr = -(G/r²) [ρ(r) + P(r)/c²] [M(r) + 4πr³P(r)/c²] [1 - 2GM(r)/c²r]⁻¹
   -								dP/dr: The pressure gradient required to resist gravitational collapse.
 								ρ(r): Energy density at radius r.
 								P(r): Pressure at radius r.
   								sM(r): Total mass enclosed within radius r.

13-14*[Permeability - refers to different concepts in physics and engineering. Below are the primary formulas used for magnetic permeability (electromagnetism) and fluid permeability (Earth sciences/fluid mechanics). 
							
							13 - Magnetic Permeability (Electromagnetism): μ = B / H
									μ = Absolute permeability (H/m)
									B = Magnetic flux density (T) Magnetic flux density (measured in Tesla).
									H = Magnetic field strength (A/m) Magnetic field strength (measured in Amperes per meter).

							14 - Relative Permeability: μᵣ = μ / μ₀]
									μ₀ = Permeability of Free Space: A dimensionless ratio of a material's absolute permeability to vacuum permeability: μ₀ = 4π · α · ħ / (e² · c) or approximately ≈ 4π × 10⁻⁷ H/m
									α  = Fine-structure constant (~1/137.036)
									ħ  = Reduced Planck constant
									e  = Elementary charge
									c  = Speed of light in a vacuum

							15 - Fluid Permeability (Darcy’s Law): permeability (\(k\)) measures how easily a fluid can pass through a porous medium like rock or soil. 
										k = (Q · μ · L) / (A · ΔP)
										k  = Permeability (m²)
										Q  = Flow rate or discharge. (m³/s)
										μ  = Dynamic viscosity of the fluid. (Pa·s)
										L  = Length of the sample (m)
										A  = Cross-sectional area (m²)
										ΔP = sApplied Pressure drop (Pa)

							16 - Membrane (Cells/Barriers) Permeability: Membrane permeability (\(P\)) describes the rate of passive diffusion of molecules across a membrane
										P = (K · D) / Δx
										P  = Permeability coefficient (cm/s or m/s)
										K  = Partition coefficient (solubility of solute in lipid vs water)
										D  = Diffusion coefficient (cm²/s or m²/s)
										Δx = Membrane thickness (cm or m)]

17-18*[Root-Mean-Square - (RMS) speed represents the speed of a particle possessing the average kinetic energy of the gas.
							
							17 - Thermodynamic RMS Speed Formula: used in physics and chemistry to relate temperature to molecular speed.
										vᵣₘₛ = √(3 · R · T / M)
										vᵣₘₛ = Root-mean-square speed (m/s)
										R    = Universal gas constant (8.314 J/mol·K)
										T    = Absolute temperature (K)
										M    = Molar mass (kg/mol)

							18 -  Molecular RMS Speed Formula: used when dealing with individual particles rather than moles. 
										vᵣₘₛ = √(3 · kᵦ · T / m)
										vᵣₘₛ = Root-mean-square speed (m/s)
										kᵦ   = Boltzmann constant (1.38 × 10⁻²³ J/K)
										T    = Absolute temperature (K)
										m    = Mass of a single molecule (kg)]

19-25*[Velocity-Formulas: 				19 - Velocity-Time Formula: Used to find the velocity after a specific time 
										v_f = v_i + (a * t)
										v_f = Final velocity 
										v_i = Initial velocity 
										a   = Acceleration 
										t   = Time (float)
												
							20 - Displacement-Velocity Formula: Used for predictive aiming or checking if a projectile can reach a tile before a timer expires.
										s = (v_i * t) + (0.5 * a * t²)
										s   = Displacement (Vector2, distance from start to target)
										v_i = Initial velocity (Vector2)
										a   = Acceleration (Vector2)
										t   = Time (float)

							21 - Velocity-Displacement (The "Jump" Formula): Crucial for calculating the exact initial velocity required to reach a specific tile height or distance without knowing the time. 
										v_f² = v_i² + 2 * a * s
										Example for Jump Velocity: v_initial_y = sqrt(2 * gravity * target_height)

							22 - Average Velocity (The "Tile Center" Formula): Used to find where an entity should be midway through a turn or move. 
										v_avg = (v_i + v_f) / 2

							23 -  Force and Mass (Newton’s Second Law): Essential for combat knockback or wind/magic pushes. It calculates the change in velocity based on the force applied to a specific mass.
										velocity += (Force / mass) * delta
										Force = Impact or push Vector2 (Newtons)
										mass  = Resistance to acceleration (kg or unitless)


							24 - Friction and Damping (Decay) - For "fire" dissipating or characters sliding to a stop, use a damping factor to reduce velocity over time. 
												velocity = velocity * pow(damping_factor, delta)
												damping_factor = Value between 0.0 and 1.0 (e.g., 0.9 for 10% loss per second)

							25 - Target Tracking (Directional Velocity): For homing magic or projectiles aiming at a target, you must normalize the direction vector to maintain a constant speed.
												velocity = (target_position - current_position).normalized() * speed
												target_position = Vector2 of the target
												speed = Constant scalar value (pixels/s)]

26-29*[Thermal-Expasnsion: thermal expansion is calculated based on whether you are measuring a change in length (1D), area (2D), or volume (3D).
							
							26 -  Linear Thermal Expansion (1D): Used for the expansion of thin objects like wires, beams, or tracks. 
												ΔL = α · L₀ · ΔT
												ΔL = Change in length (m)
												α  = Coefficient of linear expansion (1/°C or 1/K)
												L₀ = Initial length (m)
												ΔT = Change in temperature (°C or K)


							27 - Area Thermal Expansion (2D): This is the most relevant for 2D tile-based games, used to calculate how much a tile or surface expands when heated by fire. 
												ΔA = γ · A₀ · ΔT  (or ΔA = 2α · A₀ · ΔT)
												ΔA = Change in area (m²)
												γ  = Coefficient of area expansion (γ ≈ 2α)
												A₀ = Initial area (m²)
												ΔT = Change in temperature

							28 - Volumetric Thermal Expansion (3D): Used for fluids (liquids/gases) or solid 3D objects. 
												ΔV = β · V₀ · ΔT (or ΔV = 3α · V₀ · ΔT)
												ΔV = Change in volume (m³)
												β  = Coefficient of volume expansion (β ≈ 3α)
												V₀ = Initial volume (m³)
												ΔT = Change in temperature

							29 - Final Dimension Calculation: To find the new size (Length, Area, or Volume) after the expansion has occurred:
												L_final = L₀(1 + αΔT)
												A_final = A₀(1 + γΔT)
												V_final = V₀(1 + βΔT)]

30-33*[Resonance: occurs when a system is driven at its natural frequency, leading to maximum amplitude oscillations.
							
							30 - Mechanical Resonance (Spring-Mass System): for  knockback or shaking effects where an object oscillates after being hit. 
												fᵣ = (1 / 2π) · √(k / m)
												fᵣ = Resonant frequency (Hz)
												k  = Spring constant or stiffness (N/m)
												m  = Mass of the object (kg)

							31 - Electrical Resonance (LC Circuit): Use this for magic mana-recharge or signal-based puzzles where a circuit must be "tuned" to a specific frequency.
												fᵣ = 1 / (2π · √(L · C))
												fᵣ = Resonant frequency (Hz)
												L  = Inductance (Henries, H)
												C  = Capacitance (Farads, F)


							32 - Acoustic Resonance (Airtubes/Pipes): Use this for sound-based magic or environmental puzzles involving wind or pipes.
											    A - Open at Both Ends (or Fixed String):
												fₙ = (n · v) / (2 · L)
												fₙ = nth harmonic frequency (Hz)
												n  = Harmonic number (1, 2, 3...)
												v  = Speed of sound in the medium (m/s)
												L  = Length of the pipe or string (m)

											    B - Closed at One End:
												fₙ = (n · v) / (4 · L)
												n = Only odd harmonics (1, 3, 5...)
							
							33 - Quality Factor (Q-Factor): This determines how "sharp" or "forgiving" your resonance is. A high Q-factor means the player must be exactly on the right frequency to trigger the effect.
												Q = (1 / R) · √(L / C)
												R = Resistance (higher R makes resonance "blurrier" or broader)]

34-39*[Resonance Multiplier: Formally known as the Magnification Factor (\(M\)) or the Amplitude Ratio. It calculates how many times the standard displacement is multiplied when a system is driven at a specific frequency.
							
							34 - Resonance Magnification Factor (Damped System): Determines the amplitude based on how close the driving frequency is to the natural frequency.
												M = 1 / √[(1 - r²)² + (2 · ζ · r)²]
												M = Magnification Factor (The multiplier for amplitude/damage/shake)
												r = Frequency Ratio (f_driving / f_resonant)
												ζ = Damping Ratio (Zeta; 0 = no damping, 1 = critically damped)

							35 - Damped Peak Magnification Factor: This formula calculates the exact peak multiplier for a system with damping
												Mₚ = 1 / (2ζ · √(1 - ζ²))
												Mₚ = Peak Resonance Multiplier
												ζ  = Damping ratio (dimensionless)
												

							36 -  Peak Frequency Formula: The frequency at which the maximum multiplier actually occurs (which is slightly lower than the undamped natural frequency).
												fₚ = fₙ · √(1 - 2ζ²)
												fₚ = Peak frequency (Hz)
												fₙ = Natural frequency (Hz)
												ζ  = Damping ratio

							37 - Transmissibility Ratio: Used specifically to calculate the multiplier of force or displacement transmitted through a resonant base to an object.
												TR = √[1 + (2ζr)²] / √[(1 - r²)² + (2ζr)²]
												TR = Transmissibility (Multiplier)
												r  = Frequency ratio (f_driving / f_n)
												ζ  = Damping ratio

							38 - Q-Factor (Energy Multiplier): The peak multiplier expressed as the ratio of total energy stored vs. energy lost per cycle.
												Q = 1 / (2ζ)
												Q = Quality Factor (Multiplier at resonance)
												ζ = Damping ratio

							39 - Velocity Resonance Multiplier: The multiplier specifically for the velocity amplitude of a resonant system (as opposed to displacement).
												Mᵥ = 1 / √[(2ζ)² + (r - 1/r)²]
												Mᵥ = Velocity Magnification Factor
												r  = Frequency ratio (f_driving / f_n)
												ζ  = Damping ratio

40-49*[Misc.- Formulas i missed. 

							40 - Moisture Content: Calculates the percentage of water weight relative to the dry weight of a material.
												MC = ( (W_g - W_o) / W_o ) * 100
												MC  = Moisture Content (%)
												W_g = Green weight (initial weight)
												W_o = Oven-dry weight

							41 - Swelling/Shrinkage Factor: Determines the percentage change in volume (or dimension) due to hydration or dehydration.
												Sw = ( (V_g - V_d) / V_d ) * 100
												Sw  = Swelling/Shrinkage Factor (%)
												V_g = Green volume (fully hydrated volume)
												V_d = Dry volume

							42 - Specific Gravity (Gm): The ratio of the material's density (p (rho)) to the density of water (p (rho), used to assess rigidity.
													Gm = ρ_m / ρ_w
													Gm  = Specific Gravity (dimensionless)
													ρ_m = Density of the material (kg/m³)
													ρ_w = Density of water (~1000 kg/m³)

							43 - Atomic Packing Factor (APF): A theoretical measure of how efficiently atoms are packed in a crystal lattice structure.
													APF = (N_atoms * V_atom) / V_unit_cell
													APF       = Atomic Packing Factor (dimensionless, e.g., 0.74 for FCC/HCP)
													N_atoms   = Number of atoms per unit cell
													V_atom    = Volume of a single atom (4/3 * π * r³)
													V_unit_cell = Total volume of the unit cell

							44 -  Bonding Force (F_net): The net force required to break or deform metallic bonds, integrating attractive and repulsive forces over distance.
												F_net = Integral(F_A dr) + Integral(F_R dr)
												F_net = Net force required (N)
												F_A   = Attractive force
												F_R   = Repulsive force
												dr    = Change in interatomic distance

							45 -  Space-Time Interval (ds²):The fundamental "distance" formula in relativity, determining if events are time-like (causal) or space-like (simultaneous in some frame)
												ds² = -(c · dt)² + (dx² + dy² + dz²)
												ds² = The invariant space-time interval (m²)
												c = Speed of light
												dt = Time difference between events (s)
												dx,dy,dz = Spatial differences (m)
												
							46 - Relativistic Momentum (p): Momentum calculated for objects moving near the speed of light, where mass increases with velocity.
												p = γ · m · u
												p = Relativistic momentum (kg·m/s)
												γ = Lorentz factor (gamma; γ = 1 / sqrt(1 - (u²/c²)))
												m = Rest mass (kg)
												u = 3-velocity (m/s)


							47 -  Proper Time (\tau): The actual invariant time measured by a clock moving along a specific path through space-time (the time "experienced" by a player character).
												dτ = sqrt( dt² - ( (dx² + dy² + dz²) / c² ) )
												dτ = Differential of proper time (s)
												dt = Differential of coordinate time (s)
												dx,dy,dz = Differentials of spatial coordinates (m)
												c  = Speed of light]


							47B -  Chronal Acceleration (α_τ): the acceleration of an object relative to its Proper Time (τ). This formula is used to calculate the force felt by an object when time is being dilated or compressed. 
												α_τ = d²x / dτ² = γ² · a + γ⁴ · ( (v · a) / c² ) · v
												α_τ = Chronal (Proper) acceleration (m/s²)
												γ = Lorentz factor (1 / sqrt(1 - v²/c²))
												a = Coordinate acceleration
												v = Current velocity Vector2
												c = Speed of light 

							48 - Drag Coefficient (Cd): This formula isolates the drag coefficient from the standard Drag Equation. It represents how much an object's shape resists motion
												Cd = (2 · Fd) / (ρ · v² · A)
												Cd = Drag coefficient (dimensionless)
												Fd = Drag force (N)
												ρ  = Density of the fluid (kg/m³)
												v  = Velocity of the object relative to the fluid (m/s)
												A  = Reference area / Cross-sectional area (m²)

											    B - Drag Force (Opposite to Velocity):
												Fd = 0.5 · ρ · v² · Cd · A


							49 -  Lift Coefficient (Cl): This formula isolates the lift coefficient, representing the ability of a shape (like a wing or a curved magic projectile) to generate force perpendicular to the flow. 
												Cl = (2 · Fl) / (ρ · v² · A)
												Cl = Lift coefficient (dimensionless)
												Fl = Lift force (N)
												ρ  = Fluid density (kg/m³)
												v  = Velocity (m/s)
												A  = Planform area (m²)
												
											    B - Lift Force (Perpendicular to Velocity):
												Fl = 0.5 · ρ · v² · Cl · A

50-54*[Phase Coherence: Phase Coherence (\(|\gamma _{12}|\)) measures the statistical correlation between two waves (magic projectiles, light, or oscillations). A value of (1) indicates perfect coherence (constructive interference), while (0) indicates total incoherence.

							50 - Degree of Mutual Coherence (Complex Coherence): This formula calculates the correlation between two wave fields, \(E_{1}\) and \(E_{2}\), at a specific time delay (\(\tau \)). 
												γ₁₂(τ) = ⟨E₁(t) · E₂*(t + τ)⟩ / √[ ⟨|E₁(t)|²⟩ · ⟨|E₂(t)|²⟩ ]
												γ₁₂(τ) = Degree of coherence (Complex value between 0 and 1)
												E₁, E₂ = Wave amplitudes (Vector2 or Complex)
												⟨ ⟩ = Time-averaged expectation
												* = Complex conjugate
												τ = Time delay/offset 

							51 - Visibility Formula (Interference Multiplier): Used to calculate the "fringe visibility" or the intensity of the resulting interference pattern (e.g., how much damage is amplified by two overlapping magic spells).
												V = (I_max - I_min) / (I_max + I_min)
												V = Visibility (Coherence multiplier)
												I_max = Maximum intensity (Constructive interference)
												I_min = Minimum intensity (Destructive interference)


							52 - Phase Difference (Δφ): The most common implementation for calculating the instantaneous state of coherence between two synchronized sources.
												Δφ = (2π · Δx / λ) + Δφ₀
												Δφ  = Phase difference (radians)
												Δx  = Path length difference (m)
												λ   = Wavelength (m)
												Δφ₀ = Initial phase offset (radians)

							53 - Coherence Length (L_c) Determines the physical distance over which a wave (like a magic beam) maintains its coherence before becoming "chaotic." 
												L_c = c / Δf  (or L_c = λ² / Δλ)
												L_c = Coherence length (m)
												c   = Speed of the wave (m/s)
												Δf  = Frequency bandwidth (Hz)
												λ   = Central wavelength
												Δλ  = Spectral width

							54 -Coherence Multiplier for Intensity If you are calculating the combined intensity (\(I_{tot}\)) of two coherent magic sources:
												I_tot = I₁ + I₂ + 2 · sqrt(I₁ · I₂) · |γ₁₂| · cos(Δφ)
												I₁, I₂ = Intensities of individual sources
												|γ₁₂|  = Degree of coherence (Resonance/Coherence Multiplier)
												cos(Δφ)= The phase interference term]

55-*[Conductivity (σ): the measure of a material's ability to allow the flow of an electric current or heat. It is the inverse of resistivity
												
							55 -   Electrical Conductivity (Standard): This formula defines conductivity based on the physical properties of the conductor. 
												σ = L / (R · A)
												σ = Electrical conductivity (S/m - Siemens per meter)
												R = Resistance (Ω)
												A = Cross-sectional area (m²)
												L = Length of the material (m)
							
							56 - Conductivity from Resistivity The fundamental relationship between conductivity and resistivity (ρ).
												σ = 1 / ρ
												σ = Electrical conductivity (S/m)
												ρ = Resistivity (Ω·m)

							57 - Microscopic Conductivity (Drude Model): Used for Metal Nature simulations to calculate how charge carriers (electrons) move through an atomic lattice.
												σ = n · e · μ  (or σ = n · e² · τ / m)
												σ = Electrical conductivity (S/m)
												n = Charge carrier density (number of electrons/m³)
												e = Elementary charge (1.602 × 10⁻¹⁹ C)
												μ = Mobility of charge carriers (m²/V·s)
												τ = Mean free time between collisions (s)
												m = Effective mass of the carrier (kg 

							58 - Thermal Conductivity (k): In Fire or Heat systems, this formula calculates the rate at which heat energy transfers through a material. 
												k = (Q · L) / (A · ΔT · t)
												k  = Thermal conductivity (W/m·K)
												Q  = Amount of heat transferred (J)
												L  = Thickness/Length of the material (m)
												A  = Surface area (m²)
												ΔT = Temperature difference (K or °C)
												t  = Time (s)

							59 - Wiedemann–Franz Law: This relates thermal conductivity (\(\kappa \)) and electrical conductivity (\(\sigma \)) for metals, which is highly useful for 2026-standard multi-element simulations. 
												κ / σ = L · T
												κ = Thermal conductivity
												σ = Electrical conductivity
												L = Lorenz number (2.44 × 10⁻⁸ W·Ω·K⁻²)
												T = Absolute temperature (K)]

60-64*[Arc-Capacity - (often analyzed via Paschen's Law or Dielectric Strength) determines the maximum energy or voltage a gap (like a tile-space in your game) can sustain before the medium ionizes and creates a "Magic Arc" or electrical discharge.

							60 - Breakdown Voltage (Paschen’s Law): This calculates the "Arc Capacity" of a gap—the voltage required to initiate an arc across a distance (\(d\)) at a specific pressure (\(p\)).
												V_b = (B · p · d) / [ ln(A · p · d) - ln(ln(1 + 1/γ)) ]
												V_b = Breakdown voltage (The Arc Capacity limit)
												p   = Pressure (Atmospheres or Pascals)
												d = Gap distance (m)
												A,B = Material constants for the gas/medium
												γ = Townsend secondary-electron emission coefficient

							61 - Energy Capacity of an Arc: If the arc is treated as a plasma discharge, its energy capacity (\(E\)) is determined by the capacitance of the source and the voltage.
												E = 0.5 · C · V²
												E = Energy capacity (Joules)
												C = Capacitance of the "source" (Farads)
												V = Breakdown voltage (V_b)

							62 - Arc Current Capacity (Ohm’s Law for Arcs): Once the arc is formed, its capacity to carry current is governed by the ionized path's resistance.
												I_arc = (V_source - V_arc) / R_circuit
												I_arc    = Current flowing through the arc (A)
												V_source = Source voltage
												V_arc = Voltage drop across the arc (typically constant for a given length)
												R_circuit= Resistance of the remaining circuit

							63  - Thermal Arc Capacity (Ayrton’s Equation): Used to determine the stability of an arc based on its length and the power it can dissipate as heat.
												V_arc = A + B · L + (C + D · L) / I_arc
												V_arc = Voltage across the arc
												L = Length of the arc (m)
												I_arc = Arc current (A)
												A,B,C,D = Empirical constants based on electrode material (Metal Nature)


							64 - Dielectric Strength (Simplified Capacity): For quick game logic to determine if a "Magic Arc" jumps between two tiles:
												E_max = V / d
												E_max = Dielectric strength (V/m)
												V = Applied voltage
												d = Distance between Vector2 positions]

65-69*[Magnetic Susceptibility (χₘ)- a dimensionless measure of how much a material will become magnetized in an applied magnetic field. It determines the "Nature" of the material (Paramagnetic, Diamagnetic, or Ferromagnetic)

							65 - Volume Magnetic Susceptibility: This is the standard formula relating magnetization (M) to the magnetic field strength (H)]						
												χₘ = M / H
												χₘ = Volume magnetic susceptibility (dimensionless)
												M = Magnetization (magnetic dipole moment per unit volume, A/m)
												H = Magnetic field strength (A/m)

							66 - Relationship to Relative Permeability: This formula links susceptibility to the material's relative permeability (\(\mu _{r}\)), which determines how the "Metal Nature" interacts with magnetic magic or forces. 
												χₘ = μᵣ - 1
												χₘ = Magnetic susceptibility
												μᵣ = Relative permeability (dimensionless)

							67 - Mass (Gram) Magnetic Susceptibility: Used when the simulation calculates effects based on the mass of a character or object rather than its volume
												χ_mass = χₘ / ρ
												χ_mass = Mass susceptibility (m³/kg)
												χₘ = Volume susceptibility
												ρ = Density (kg/m³)

							68 - Molar Magnetic Susceptibility: Used for atomic-level calculations or specific material "recipes" in your crafting system.
												χ_molar = χ_mass · M_m
												χ_molar = Molar susceptibility (m³/mol)
												M_m = Molar mass (kg/mol)

							69 - Curie’s Law (Temperature Dependency): Essential for "Fire" vs. "Metal" interactions. As the temperature (\(T\)) of a paramagnetic material increases, its magnetic susceptibility decreases.
												χₘ = C / T
												χₘ = Magnetic susceptibility
												C = Material-specific Curie constant
												T = Absolute temperature (K)]

70-*[Ion-Density (nᵢ): measures the number of ions per unit volume. this is used to determine the potency of "Magic Arcs," the conductivity of "Fire" (plasma), or the behavior of ionized gases

							70 - Basic Ion Density (Volumetric): This formula calculates the concentration of ions within a given space (V)
												nᵢ = Nᵢ / V
												nᵢ = Ion density (ions/m³)
												Nᵢ = Total number of ions	
												V  = Volume (m³)

							71 - Ion Density from Charge Density: Ion density is often derived from the total volumetric charge (\(\rho \)) and the average ionic charge (\(Z_{e}\)).
												nᵢ = ρ / (Z · e)
												nᵢ = Ion density (m⁻³)
												ρ = Volumetric charge density (C/m³)
												Z = Ionization state (e.g., 1 for singly ionized, 2 for doubly ionized)
												e = Elementary charge (1.602 × 10⁻¹⁹ C)

							72 - Degree of Ionization (Saha Equation Approximation): Used for Fire and Magic Arc systems to calculate the density of ions created by thermal energy (Heat).
												nᵢ ≈ sqrt( n_gas · ( (2π · mₑ · k_B · T) / h² )¹·⁵ · exp(-Eᵢ / (k_B · T)) )
												nᵢ = Ion density (m⁻³)
												n_gas = Neutral gas density
												mₑ  = Mass of an electron
												k_B = Boltzmann constant
												T = Absolute temperature (K)
												Eᵢ = Ionization energy of the material (Joules)
												h = Planck's constant

							73 -  Plasma Frequency Relation:Ion density can be calculated based on the observed Plasma Frequency (\(\omega _{p}\)), which determines how "Magic Arcs" oscillate.
												nᵢ = (ωₚ² · mᵢ · ε₀) / (Z² · e²)
												nᵢ  = Ion density (m⁻³)
												ωₚ  = Plasma oscillation frequency (rad/s)
												mᵢ  = Mass of the ion (kg)
												ε₀  = Permittivity of free space
												Z   = Ionization state
												e   = Elementary charge

							74 - Current Density Relationship - Used to determine how much "Magic Arc" current can flow through a tile based on the ion density and their drift velocity.
												Jᵢ = nᵢ · Z · e · v_d
												Jᵢ  = Ion current density (A/m²)
												nᵢ  = Ion density (m⁻³)
												v_d = Ion drift velocity (m/s)]

75-*[ Event Density (ρₑ):  used to measure the frequency of discrete physical occurrences (like magic impacts, particle collisions, or combat ticks) within a specific region of space-time

							75 - Volumetric Event Density: Used to determine the "chaos level" of a specific tile or area based on how many physical events are occurring within its bounds.
												ρₑ = Nₑ / (A · Δt)
												ρₑ = Event Density (events per m² per second)
												Nₑ = Total number of discrete events (hits, triggers, sparks)
												A  = Area of the 2D tile or region (m²)
												Δt = Time interval / duration (s)

							76 - Space-Time Event Density (Relativistic): Used for Time & Space mechanics to determine if a region of space is "overloaded" by events relative to the Proper Time 
												ρ_τ = Nₑ / (V_spatial · Δτ)
												ρ_τ = Proper Event Density
												V_spatial = Spatial volume (dx · dy)
												Δτ = Proper Time interval (The time experienced by the target)

							77 - Probability of Interaction (Collision Density): Used for Fire and Magic Arc systems to calculate the likelihood of a chain reaction (e.g., fire spreading or an arc jumping).
												Pₑ = ρₑ · σ_cross · Δx
												Pₑ = Probability of an event occurring
												ρₑ = Event density (particle/ion density)
												σ_cross = Interaction cross-section (the "size" of the target's hitbox)
												Δx = Distance traveled by the projectile/spark

							78 - Critical Event Threshold: use this to calculate if a material (Metal or Wood) fails due to the sheer frequency of impacts, even if a single hit doesn't exceed the Tensile Strength
												D_accum = Integral( ρₑ(t) · E_event dt )
												D_accum = Accumulated damage/stress
												ρₑ(t)   = Event density over time
												E_event = Energy per individual event]
												*[Critical Event Threshold: Notes-from Ai on design -Performance Scaling: If ρₑ in a specific Vector2 region exceeds a CPU threshold, use it to trigger "Event Merging" (combining 10 small fire particles into 1 large fire area-of-effect) to save processing power.
													Shatter Logic: If ρₑ exceeds the Plastic Strain Rate's recovery time, the material (Metal) enters a state of "Fatigue" and shatters regardless of individual force magnitudes.]

79-*[Reflectance (R):  define the visual interaction with light [determines how "shiny"]

							79 - Reflectance: calculates the ratio of reflected light power to incident light power.
												R = | (n₁ - n₂) / (n₁ + n₂) |²
												R  = Reflectance (0 to 1)
												n₁ = Refractive index of the first medium (Air ≈ 1.0)
												n₂ = Refractive index of the material (e.g., Iron ≈ 2.9, Wood ≈ 1.5)

								For Metallic Reflectance (including absorption):
												R = [ (n - 1)² + k² ] / [ (n + 1)² + k² ]
												k = Extinction coefficient (absorption rate of the metal) 

							80 - Specular Reflection Vector: calculate the resulting Vector2 of a light ray or magic beam bouncing off a surface.
												r = i - 2(i · n)n
												r = Reflection Vector2
												i = Incident (incoming) Vector2
												n = Surface Normal Vector2 (perpendicular to the tile edge)]

81-*[Atomic Packing: structural integrity of solids

							81 - Atomic Packing Factor (\(APF\)): measures the density of a crystal lattice. It is the primary "Metal Nature" constant that determines theoretical hardness and the Shatter vs. Deform threshold.
												APF = (N_atoms · V_atom) / V_unit_cell
												APF = Atomic Packing Factor (e.g., 0.74 for Gold/Lead, 0.68 for Iron)
												N_atoms = Number of atoms in the unit cell
												V_atom = Volume of a single atom ( (4/3) · π · r³ )
												V_unit_cell = Total volume of the unit cell lattice

							82 - Atomic Density (\(\rho _{at}\)): Used calculate the Ion Density or Event Density specifically within a metal tile's lattice.
												ρ_at = (n · A) / (V_c · N_A)
												n = Number of atoms per unit cell
												A = Atomic weight
												V_c = Volume of the unit cell
												N_A = Avogadro's number

82-*[Positive-Curse-Energy-Formulas:
							83 - Stamina Restoration (The Efficiency Formula): This formula calculates how much "Exhaustion Drag" is removed from the target. 
												R = Magnitude * (1 / ζ)
												R = Restoration Rate (The speed/velocity of recovery)
												Magnitude = The initial "Debt" or "Displacement" (How much damage/change occurred)
												ζ = Damping Ratio (The resistance to movement/change)

							84 -  Application: Structural Recovery (Metal/Wood): Used to calculate how fast a material "snaps back" from Tensile Strain or Plastic Strain.
												R_structural = (ΔL) * (1 / ζ)
												ΔL = The current deformation (displacement from rest)
												ζ  = Internal friction of the material (e.g., 0.05 for Steel, 0.4 for Wet Wood)

							85 - Application: Mana/Energy Recharge - Used for the Arc-Capacity or Conductivity systems to determine how fast a tile's ionized state neutralizes after a magic arc discharge.
												R_mana = (Energy_Deficit) * (1 / ζ_circuit)
												ζ_circuit = The electrical damping (proportional to Resistivity ρ)

							86 - Application: Chronal Stasis Recovery Used for Time & Space mechanics to determine how fast the Space-Time Interval (\(ds^{2}\)) returns to normal after a relativistic event.
												R_time = (Temporal_Dilation) * (1 / ζ_space)

							87 - Detoxification (The Osmotic Flush): This formula calculates the velocity at which toxins are removed from the cellular structure.
												P_detox = ( (K + M) · D ) / Δx
												P_detox = Accelerated Permeability coefficient (cm/s)
												K = Partition coefficient (solubility of toxin)
												M = Spell Magnitude (The "force" added to the permeability)
												D = Diffusion coefficient
												Δx = Membrane thickness

							88 -  The Flush Rate (Mass Flux): To determine the actual amount of toxin removed per second, use Fick’s First Law integrated with your accelerated permeability.
												J = P_detox · (C_cell - C_flush)
												J = Flush Rate (Amount of toxin moved per unit area per second)
												C_cell = Concentration of poison inside the cell
												C_flush = Concentration of the "cleaning" medium (assumed to be 0 or low)

							89 -  Neutralization Logic (Threshold Check): This is the mechanical trigger used to determine if the poison effect is immediately deleted or merely reduced.
												If (M_detox > M_poison):
    											State = Neutralized (Toxin concentration = 0)
													Else:
    												Toxin_Concentration -= (J * delta)

90-**[Negative-Curse-Energy-Formulas:
							90 - Magic Fatigue Rate (\(F\)): This formula is the inverse of the Restoration Rate. It represents how magic "clogs" or "tires" a system by artificially inflating the damping (\(\zeta \)), making recovery increasingly difficult.
												F = Magnitude · ζ
												F = Fatigue Rate (The speed of degradation)
												Magnitude = The intensity of the magic influence
												ζ = Damping Ratio (The system's inherent resistance)

							91 -  Accumulated Fatigue (The Debt): To calculate the total fatigue over a spell duration, you integrate the Fatigue Rate. This represents the "permanent" or "long-term" damage that lowers the effective Restoration Rate for subsequent turns..
												D_fatigue = Integral( F(t) dt )
												D_fatigue = Total accumulated fatigue (The offset to equilibrium)
												F(t) = Instantaneous fatigue rate

							92 -  Effective Recovery (\(R_{eff}\)) When a system is under both Restoration and Fatigue (e.g., a character trying to heal while cursed), the net movement is the difference between the two.
												R_eff = (Magnitude_heal / ζ) - (Magnitude_fatigue · ζ)
												R_eff > 0: System is recovering
												R_eff < 0: System is succumbing to fatigue

91-*[Air Density: To model air density (\(\rho \)) relative to temperature (\(T\)), pressure (\(p\)), and humidity, the most accurate approach is to treat air as a mixture of dry air and water vapor

							93 - Core Air Density Formula: (Moist Air) Calculates the total density (\(\rho \)) by summing the individual densities of dry air and water vapor.
												ρ = (p_d / (R_d · T)) + (p_v / (R_v · T))
												ρ   = Total air density (kg/m³)
												p_d = Partial pressure of dry air (Pa)
												p_v = Partial pressure of water vapor (Pa)
												T = Absolute temperature (K)
												R_d = Gas constant for dry air (287.058 J/(kg·K))
												R_v = Gas constant for water vapor (461.495 J/(kg·K))]

							94 - Modeling for Altitude: Used to adjust baseline pressure and temperature based on the character's height (\(h\)) relative to sea level.
												Step A: Pressure at Altitude (\(p\))
												p = p₀ · (1 - (L · h) / T₀) ^ ((g · M) / (R · L))
												p = Atmospheric pressure at altitude (Pa)
												p₀ = Sea level standard pressure (101,325 Pa)
												T₀ = Sea level standard temperature (288.15 K)
												L = Temperature lapse rate (0.0065 K/m)
												h = Altitude (m) [Negative for below sea level]
												g = Gravitational acceleration (9.80665 m/s²)
												M = Molar mass of Earth's air (0.0289644 kg/mol)
												R = Universal gas constant (8.3144598 J/(mol·K))

												Step B: Temperature at Altitude (\(T\))
												T = T₀ - (L · h)
												T = Standard temperature at altitude (K)

							95 - Incorporating Humidity: Adjusts the air density calculation based on water vapor content, which makes air lighter.
												Saturation Vapor Pressure (\(p_{sat}\)) 
												p_sat = 610.78 · 10 ^ ((7.5 · Tc) / (Tc + 237.3))
												p_sat = Saturation vapor pressure (Pa)
												Tc = Temperature in Celsius (°C)

												Actual Vapor Pressure (\(p_{v}\)) and Dry Air Pressure (\(p_{d}\))
												p_v = RH · p_sat
												p_d = p - p_v
												RH = Relative Humidity (expressed as a decimal, e.g., 0.50 for 50%)
												p  = Total atmospheric pressure calculated in Step 2A

							97-*[Combat Formulas and liquid conversion: Move from Character System doc:
                                         
													Liquid Conversion
													1 mL= .271 Dram
													1 Dram = 3.69 mL 
													Weight = Volume (mL) x Density


							98. -[Diffusion Rate: Fick's First Law (Steady-State Diffusion):

													J = -D * (dC / dx)
													J: Diffusion flux (amount of substance per unit area per unit time)
													D: Diffusion coefficient (m²/s)
													dC/dx: Concentration gradient (change in concentration over distance)

										Fick's Second Law (Non-Steady-State Diffusion):
													∂C / ∂t = D * (∂²C / ∂x²)
													∂C/∂t: Change in concentration over time
													∂²C/∂x²: The second derivative (curvature) of concentration with respect to position]

							99- [Entropy Formulas: 

										 Thermodynamic Entropy (Clausius):
													ΔS = Q_rev / T
							 						ΔS: Change in entropy (J/K)
													Q_rev: Heat exchanged in a reversible process (Joules)
													T: Absolute temperature (Kelvin)

										Statistical Entropy (Boltzmann):
													S = k_B * ln(W)
													S: Absolute entropy
													k_B: Boltzmann constant (1.38 x 10⁻²³ J/K)
													W (or Ω): Number of microstates (configurations)
										ln: Natural logarithm

										 Statistical Entropy (Gibbs):
													S = -k_B * Σ (p_i * ln(p_i))
													p_i: Probability of the system being in microstate 'i'
													Σ: Summation over all possible microstates

										Information Entropy (Shannon):
													H = -Σ (p_i * log_b(p_i))
													H: Information entropy (bits if base b=2)
													p_i: Probability of outcome 'i'
													log_b: Logarithm to base 'b']

							100- [NIOSH Lifting Equation: May need Abstraction, use this to calculate the Recommended Weight Limit (RWL) for manual lifting.

										RWL = LC × HM × VM × DM × AM × FM × CM

												Where:
											LC (Load Constant) = 51 lbs (23 kg)
											HM (Horizontal Multiplier) = 10/H (H = distance from body)
											VM (Vertical Multiplier) = 1-(.0075|V-30|) (V = start height)
											DM (Distance Multiplier) = .82 + (1.8/D) (D = travel distance)
											AM (Asymmetric Multiplier) = 1-(.0032A) (A = angle of twist)
											FM (Frequency Multiplier) = (From NIOSH frequency tables)
											CM (Coupling Multiplier) = (Based on grip/handle quality)

							101- [The Leverage Force Formula (Law of the Lever) standard formula for leverage in physics, Archimedes'Law of the Lever, 
										relates the forces and the distances from the fulcrum (pivot point):

`											Effort Force * Effort Arm Length = Load Force * Load Arm Length`

							commonly expressed using the balance of **torque** (rotational force) on either side of the fulcrum. The formula is:

`											Fe * de = Fl * dl`

												Where:
											Fe = Effort force (the force you apply)
											de = Distance from the fulcrum to where the effort force is applied (effort arm)
											Fl = Load force (the weight or resistance being moved)
											dl = Distance from the fulcrum to the load force (load arm)

									Rearranged to solve for effort force required:

`											Fe = (Fl * dl) / de`

					This shows that the longer the effort arm relative to the load arm, the less force (**Fe**) you need to apply to move the load (**Fl**)]

*   Median Infectious Dose (ID50) Spearman–Kärber Method:
    log ID50 = log(highest dilution giving 100% CPE) + 0.5 - (total number of test units showing CPE / number of test units per dilution)
*   Multiplicity of Infection (MOI) (Cell Culture):
    MOI = Number of viral particles used per well / Number of cells originally seeded in the well
*   Plaque Assay Titer:
    Titer (PFU/ml) = Plaques counted * (1 / dilution) * volume correction

CPE(Cytopathic Effect) - The observable damage or morphological changes a virus causes to host cells in a culture.

## Multiplier During Illness (Viral/Bacterial Growth)

*   Viral Load (from PCR Ct value):
    viral RNA copies per mL = 133.3333 * e^((37.933 - Ct) / 1.418)
*   Bacterial Growth Rate (k) (generations/unit time):
    k = log10(Nt / N0) / (0.301 * t)
*   Bacterial Number (exponential growth):
    Nt = N0 * 2^n
    or
    Nt = N t = N0 * 10^(Kt)
    or
    N t = N0 * e^(Kt)
    (Where n is the number of generations, and K is the growth rate constant.)

## Load Value for Passing It On (Transmission Threshold)

*   Basic Reproduction Number (R0) (from transmission rate beta and removal rate gamma):
    R0 = beta / gamma
    (Alternatively: R0 = tau * c_bar * d (transmissibility tau, average contact rate c_bar, duration of infectiousness d))
*   Basic Reproduction Number (from exponential growth rate r and generation time distribution g(tau)):
    R0_hat = 1 / Integral[g(tau) * exp(-r*tau) d(tau)]
*   Viral Dynamics Model (R0):
    R0 = lambda * beta * k / (dT * dI * c)
    (lambda = target cell production rate, beta = infection rate, k = virus production rate, dT = target cell death, dI = infected cell death, c = virus clearance rate.)

# Formulas and Definitions (Reproduction Rate)

## Basic Reproduction Number (R0)

R0 is a theoretical, dimensionless number representing the average number of new infections caused by one infected person in a completely susceptible population with no interventions in place.

*   **Formula 1:**
    R0 = tau * c_bar * d
    (tau = transmissibility; c_bar = average rate of contact; d = duration of infectiousness)
*   **Formula 2 (from SIR model):**
    R0 = beta / gamma
    (beta = transmission rate; gamma = removal rate, or 1/d)

## Effective Reproduction Number (Rt or Re)

Rt measures the actual transmission potential of a disease at a specific time t in a  population, considering existing immunity levels, vaccination coverage, and ongoing control measures.

*   **Formula:**
    Rt = R0 * S/N
    (S = number of susceptible individuals; N = total population size)

### Interpretation

*   If R0 or Rt > 1: disease continues to spread and grow.
*   If R0 or Rt < 1: disease spread slows down and eventually dies out.

# Illness Recovery Drift Formula

This formula calculates the amount of Infection_Load that the character's immune system eliminates during a given time period (e.g., per turn or per hour), using the character's existing stats.

*   **Infection_Load_Decrease** = MAX(1, (Current_Infection_Load / (Constitution + Resilience))) * (1 / (1 + (Time_Exposed / Recovery_Constant)))

--------------------------
Container Volume (Physical Space)
--- Rectangular (Box/Bin) ---
Volume = Length × Width × Height

--- Cylindrical (Bucket/Jar) ---
Volume = π × radius² × Height 
(radius = 1/2 of the diameter)

--- Irregular or "Packed" Items ---
Number of Items = Container Volume / Individual Item Volume
*Note: This doesn't account for "air gaps." For realism, multiply by 0.75-0.80
